  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText18021251459311541410" style="display:none">Dying of a broken heart is just the beginning.... Welcome to forever. <br /><br />Brie's life ends at sixteen: Her boyfriend tells her he doesn't love her, and the news breaks her heart—literally. <br /><br />But now that she's D&amp;G (dead and gone), Brie is about to discover that love is way more complicated than she ever imagined. Back in Half Moon Bay, her family has begun to unravel. Her best friend has been keeping a secret about Jacob, the boy she loved and lost—and the truth behind his shattering betrayal. And then there's Patrick, Brie's mysterious new guide and resident Lost Soul . . . who just might hold the key to her forever after. <br /><br />With Patrick's help, Brie will have to pass through the five stages of grief before she's ready to move on. But how do you begin again, when your heart is still in pieces?</span>

This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/237709-i-am-just-confuse-with-the-lily-part-when"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I am just confuse with the Lily part, when Lily died and was reincarnated as Brie why did she come back on the year 1994? Why didn't she wait for Patrick in the after life considering that Patrick died only 7 days after her death? If Lily borrowed a soul then she died as Brie again isn't Brie considered as a lost soul also? Or I just didn't understand that part? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/42840404-jen"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/42840404-jen">Jen</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Lily died then Patrick died. Then Patrick felt bad that he caused lily to die so he gave her his soul so she would reincarnate cuz he thought she need<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Lily died then Patrick died. Then Patrick felt bad that he caused lily to die so he gave her his soul so she would reincarnate cuz he thought she needed a "second chance" in life. So by giving up his salvation, as used in the book, or soul for lily, he became a lost soul. But since lily didn't give up any soul she is not a lost soul when she was reincarnated as Brie. Plus he probably lived in the afterlife with lily for a while before deciding she should be reincarnated.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141334479" href="/book/show/13411612-the-catastrophic-history-of-you-and-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=debut-author">debut-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=i-see-dead-people">i-see-dead-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=totally-saw-that-coming">totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2012">arc-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267487836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10822324183327003705">Confession time: I was pretty sure I would love this book even before it showed up in my mailbox. I loved the title, I liked the cover, and the description sounded really interesting. What I didn’t know, however, was that I wasn’t just signing up for a fun read, I was signing up for heartbreak and some really huge, eye opening lessons. Don’t get me wrong: The Catastrophic History of You and Me is often laugh-out-loud funny, but that’s not nearly all it is. <br/> <br/>Brie Eagan’s life was perfect: she had</span>
  <span id="freeText10822324183327003705" style="display:none">Confession time: I was pretty sure I would love this book even before it showed up in my mailbox. I loved the title, I liked the cover, and the description sounded really interesting. What I didn’t know, however, was that I wasn’t just signing up for a fun read, I was signing up for heartbreak and some really huge, eye opening lessons. Don’t get me wrong: The Catastrophic History of You and Me is often laugh-out-loud funny, but that’s not nearly all it is. <br /> <br />Brie Eagan’s life was perfect: she had a great family, her three best friends and the most wonderful boyfriend a girl could wish for. At least that’s what she thought. But days before her sweet sixteen, her boyfriend Jacob uttered four horrible words that killed Brie on the spot: <b>I don’t love you</b>. It would seem that a young and perfectly healthy person really can die of a broken heart. It didn’t matter that Brie’s father is a famous cardiologist. It didn’t matter that she had so many other things to be happy about. The shock and the hurt of Jacob’s words were too much for Brie’s heart to handle. <br /><br />At the beginning of our story, Brie opens her eyes to discover that she’s indeed dead, and currently existing in her own version of afterlife, which just happens to be her family’s favorite pizza place. Her company is even more surprising, especially the boy dressed exactly like Tom Cruise in Top Gun. His name is Patrick and he immediately jumps at the chance to be Brie’s guide through afterlife, or at least this part of it. He is kind, thoughtful and the closest thing to an angel Brie is likely to meet. As the two of them go back to observe the aftermath of her death, Brie is forced to accept that her life wasn’t nearly as perfect as she thought it was and slowly fight her way through five stages of grief. <br />Here’s just a small taste of <b>denial</b>: <br /><b><i>This is all just a bad dream</i>, I told myself. <i>I’m totally in bed, totally safe, totally snuggled. Hamloaf’s next to me. Jack’s down the hall. Everything is okay.</i><br />But still, why the crazy nightmare? I must have eaten something funky. Or maybe I have a history test coming up. Or I’d forgotten to floss.</b><br /><br />In my experience, books that strike me the most are the ones that successfully mix humor and tragedy. One of the recent stellar examples is Looking for Alaska. Jess Rothenberg does this extraordinarily well. She knows when to lighten the mood with a joke, and when to stop with the humor entirely. She knows exactly how much tragedy her reader can take and when it’s time to water it down with one of Patrick’s nicknames for Brie or something similar. It is a valuable skill, and one that pretty much guarantees that I’ll read her next novel, and the one after that.<br /><br />Here’s another thing I should mention, one I’m pretty sure some of my friends will appreciate. (I won’t be naming names, though.) Seeing as Patrick had died in the 80s and he’s dressed according to the fashion of 1983 or so, every chapter is titled after a song, a huge part of them from the 80s, and there is a four-page long playlist at the end of the book. I played most of them while reading this book and felt like a lost time traveler most of the time – but in a very good way. <br /><br /><i>An advanced copy of this book was kindly provided by the publisher, Puffin/Razorbill UK for review purposes.</i><br /><br />For this review and more, please visit <a href="http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10822324183327003705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer478872730485412871"><br/>I’ll go straight to the point. Despite some reviews that say this is corny and melodramatic, I loved it, loved absolutely every word from the very beginning up to the very last word of the Acknowledgement.^^<br/><br/> “REVENGE MAY BE SWEET, BUT BOOK DEALS ARE DEFINITELY SWEETER.”<br/><br/>To me, it’s a beautiful and quirky (two adjectives you don't see together often) novel about heartbreak in all its possible meanings. It’s mysterious, fantastical, very intriguing, romantic, seriously funny (certainly had dozens a</span>
  <span id="freeText478872730485412871" style="display:none"><br />I’ll go straight to the point. Despite some reviews that say this is corny and melodramatic, I loved it, loved absolutely every word from the very beginning up to the very last word of the Acknowledgement.^^<br /><br /> “REVENGE MAY BE SWEET, BUT BOOK DEALS ARE DEFINITELY SWEETER.”<br /><br />To me, it’s a beautiful and quirky (two adjectives you don't see together often) novel about heartbreak in all its possible meanings. It’s mysterious, fantastical, very intriguing, romantic, seriously funny (certainly had dozens and dozens of lol moments like “R to the I to the P”) and utterly heartbreaking (the friends ritual at the beach had me choking on this huge lump in my throat), IT REALLY IS UNIQUELY CATASTROPHIC and IN A GOOD WAY. <br /><br />All the elements perfectly blend in from the narrative method, tone and everything else. I loved that it reads more like a fantasy book than anything else and that’s why I completely enjoyed it. I enjoyed all those pop references (Friends reference for the win. I sing smelly cat all too like all the time. Lol!) and I adore the song titles for every chapter. I keep guessing what a chapter is about based on the song title. Sorry about this useless review (if it could even be called that). You’re just going to have to read the book to know what I’m gushing about here. <br /><br />A late birthday review present to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32601463-gi" rel="nofollow noopener">Gi</a> (do check out her review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1056481500?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>). Hope you're doing great, my dear friend. &lt;3</span>

<div id="review_211620249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211620249" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211620249?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211620249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10620951089363781116"><i>“The trouble is, sometimes words are like arrows. <br/>Once you shoot them, there's no going back.”</i><br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jess-rothenberg/review-the-catastrophic-history-of-you-and-me.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359428i/710463.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>I love books that make me feel more than one emotion.. I love it when my chest feels tight and achey for a moment, and then it gets all sweet and giggly; when I want to cry and smile at the same time; when I feel like I can't get enough from the story and I would like to keep reading about the characters until the end of time.<br/><br/>This goes for this story, this goes for Brie and Patrick, for a heart whic</span>
  <span id="freeText10620951089363781116" style="display:none"><i>“The trouble is, sometimes words are like arrows. <br>Once you shoot them, there's no going back.”</i><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jess-rothenberg/review-the-catastrophic-history-of-you-and-me.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359428i/710463.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I love books that make me feel more than one emotion.. I love it when my chest feels tight and achey for a moment, and then it gets all sweet and giggly; when I want to cry and smile at the same time; when I feel like I can't get enough from the story and I would like to keep reading about the characters until the end of time.<br><br>This goes for this story, this goes for Brie and Patrick, for a heart which continues to beat, even though it has been broken in two.<br><br>The story is really heartwarming from the very beginning: Brie's heart breaks (literally and figuratively) and now - in the afterlife - she needs to find a way to let go, to move on to the other side. She finds herself in a 'tasty' version of Heaven - her favorite pizza place where she used to go with her family -  and it is not her Heaven alone. There are more kids like herself in there, but there is only one that gets her full attention, one that might have the power to make her feel 'alive' again (don't be anxious - I'll get to <em>that</em> in just a moment).<br><br><a href="http://andersonmahanski.deviantart.com/art/Who-wants-a-pizza-183950156" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359428i/710464.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="245" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What I liked about this story is the fact that it was not as predictable as I thought it would be.<br>There were some twists that I didn't see coming, and they really got to change the course of things. I will leave to you the pleasure to find all about them, still I will say a few words about some of the characters:<br><br><b>Brie:</b><br>It was easy to care for her - lost, alone, wanting her life back, angry with the whole damn universe but having a big heart (oh well, broken but still big and full of emotions)... You can easily relate to her pain and struggle, and even though she is a bit of a brat at times, you get to care for her with every page.<br><br>There are these steps a dead person goes through in order to move on, and I could see her change from one stage to the other, and more important I could understand why.<br>It was hard for her not to be with the people she loved, but it was even harder for her to witness how all their lives have changed after her death.<br><br>Somehow everything seemed to go terribly wrong and she would have given everything to make them right again. If at the beginning all she wanted was to find out "why", and it was all about finding the missing pieces from this puzzle called 'life without Brie', at the end she just needed to find out "how" to put back together those broken pieces.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“Turns out, hell's not so much a burning, scalding pit of fire and misery. It's actually much, much worse than that. Hell is when the people you love the most reach right into your soul and rip it out of you. And they do it because they can.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://photography.nationalgeographic.com/photography/photo-tips/city-photos" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359428i/710465.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="184" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Patrick:</b><br>Dressed like someone from the '80s and apparently having nothing better to do than to 'annoy' Brie, Patrick is the one that will help her find her way, the one that will give her advices when she needs one, the one to hold her in his arms when she feels more broken and lonely than ever, he is the one to cheer her up... yeah, you are right, he could be <em>the one</em>. But things are complicated (catastrophic at times), and if they are not, Brie will take care of that.<br><br>There are some things I really liked about his relation with Brie:<br>- the way he tried to help her, even when she didn't want him to;<br>- the cheese-y nicknames he picked;<br>- the way he called her Angel, and how much affection he put into that simple word;<br>Also the fights they had were amazingly cute and they made me laugh on so many times.<br><br><a href="http://emanesque.deviantart.com/art/Friends-97110171" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359428i/710466.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="202" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Brie's friends:</b><br>When Brie was alive, she had 3 best friends and a lovely boyfriend. You would think that she has lost them the moment she died, but the truth is that she will lose them all over again in her after-life. There are things that come back to her to haunt her, there are secrets that could have changed everything, and there are things that are not what you think they are.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>“You can obsess and obsess over how things ended- what you did wrong or could have done differently- but there's not much of a point. It's not like it'll change anything. So really, why worry?”</em>
</blockquote><br><br>I also loved all the <strong>musical references</strong> because they got straight to my heart.<br>Maybe it is because these are some of the songs I used to listen to in high-school, so I felt somehow closer to the character this way (take for example "It must have been love".. I so remember singing away my pain the first time my heart broke from too-much-loving and too-little-being-loved). I hope you'll enjoy them all as well.<br><br>Now... there were some things that bugged me (that's why the 4stars rating) but they won't make sense for you if you haven't read the book so please skip them, as they are a bit spoilery too:<br>- The interaction with the real world <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ not only moving some things and opening windows, but also hiding objects? Now, really? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>- Lily's story <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ if she saw what happened on Earth (because she could watch over the loved ones) why didn't she know he wouldn't live without her? Why wouldn't she wait? And what soul did she trade to come back to life <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Anyways, I loved this book and I will definitely read some more from Jess in the future!<br>Happy midnight reading, everyone!<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jess-rothenberg/review-the-catastrophic-history-of-you-and-me.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jess-rothenberg/review-the-catastrophic-history-of-you-and-me.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Lucille" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2364631-lucille"><img alt="Lucille" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440217841p2/2364631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272515930?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucille" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucille" href="/user/show/2364631-lucille">Lucille</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272515930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14931951074813723357"><blockquote>
  <b>“My heart didn't fail, someone failed my heart.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>Brie's boyfriend tells her he doesn't love her, and the news breaks her heart—literally.</i><br/><br/>If this happens in real life, I think 50% of the world's population would go down. Humans would go extinct. And <i>Delirium</i> comes in. There would be a cure for love to prevent heartbreak. Lol.<br/><br/>This was definitely a very great book. At first, I thought it was about angels and afterlife and heaven, that kind of stuff. But I was wrong. This book is about moving on,</span>
  <span id="freeText14931951074813723357" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“My heart didn't fail, someone failed my heart.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Brie's boyfriend tells her he doesn't love her, and the news breaks her heart—literally.</i><br /><br />If this happens in real life, I think 50% of the world's population would go down. Humans would go extinct. And <i>Delirium</i> comes in. There would be a cure for love to prevent heartbreak. Lol.<br /><br />This was definitely a very great book. At first, I thought it was about angels and afterlife and heaven, that kind of stuff. But I was wrong. This book is about moving on, forgiving, accepting, and most importantly, loving again. <br /><br />This book made me sad, teary, happy, laugh, smile, and of course, it left me awwww-ing at the end. Truly, love is the best part of any story (taken from Stephenie Meyer's dedication in her book, <i>The Host</i>). <br /><br />I almost cried when Brie saw her family and how she reacted. It's so relateable, since I'm 15, too, and I would hate it if my bestfriend steals my boyfriend. I would cry and scream and be sad and angry. <br /><br />I fell in love with the characters, especially sweet old Patrick Darling. I love his humor. Even though he's old, he's hilarious and super duper sweet. <br /><br />Anyway, after thinking it through, I've decided to give this book 4 stars because: a) I didn't like how Brie acted towards sweet Patrick at the end, and b) Brie died because of a stupid reason, she should have heard Jacob out first before dying, c) Jacob said the crappiest break-up line ever, d) I don't buy the reincarnation stuff. <br /><br />Notable quotes: <br /><br /><blockquote>“No matter how much you think you know a person - no matter how pretty they act, or how popular they seem, you can never know what their lives are really like.” <br /><br />“The problem is there's absolutely nothing 'fun' about falling in love. Nope. Mostly it just makes you feel sick and crazy and anxious and nervous that it's going to end miserably and ruin your whole life. And guess what: Then it does.” <br /><br />“Time doesn't necessarily heal all wounds. Sometimes, it just makes the wound worse.” <br /><br />“Hell is when the people you love the most reach right into your soul and rip it out of you. And they do it because they can.”</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14931951074813723357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Rachel Maniacup" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37103769-rachel-maniacup"><img alt="Rachel Maniacup" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516663451p2/37103769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142423905" href="/book/show/15812752-the-catastrophic-history-of-you-and-me">review of another edition</a>

      <a href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=entertaining">entertaining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37103769-rachel-maniacup?shelf=surprisingly-very-good">surprisingly-very-good</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687256728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4888791878457870143"><br/>Every time I read a book by an author I haven't encountered yet, It fascinates me because It does surprise me really good,especially when I don't really know what to expect. And I'm glad I've read this one 'cause this is something different..something you would call an amazingly unique story!<br/><br/>From the cover,the concept,the heartbreak,the romance,the humor,the drama,and particularly from the 80's pop songs that the author used as the titles of each chapter made this book incredibly adorable and me</span>
  <span id="freeText4888791878457870143" style="display:none"><br>Every time I read a book by an author I haven't encountered yet, It fascinates me because It does surprise me really good,especially when I don't really know what to expect. And I'm glad I've read this one 'cause this is something different..something you would call an amazingly unique story!<br><br>From the cover,the concept,the heartbreak,the romance,the humor,the drama,and particularly from the 80's pop songs that the author used as the titles of each chapter made this book incredibly adorable and memorable. This is a story of a 15 year old girl(turning sixteen) <b>BRIE</b>,who literally died of a broken heart when her boyfriend <b>Jacob</b> told her he doesn't love her. But when she died,it was actually just the beginning of her journey and adventures embarking on the 5 stages of grief.<br><br>I did adore this book and the characters,especially Brie's bff's Tess, Emma and Sadie.But who I did love most was HAMLOAF! I also love an ending where there's a shocking twists and turns,especially when I've discovered Jacob and Patrick's secrets! Boy,I didn't really see it coming! And though I did like Brie,I found her to be annoying because she was a bit mean and was so vengeful,that made me give this book a 4-star rating. Overall,this was an enjoyable read and I would definitely read more of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3415819.Jess_Rothenberg" title="Jess Rothenberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Jess Rothenberg</a>,and I would recommend this book to everyone!^^<br><br>Thank you so much to my friend, <b>PEARL</b> who inspired me to read this book and who is now celebrating her birthday!Please do check her lovely review on this one,too.. <b>HAPPY,HAPPY BIRTHDAY MY DEAR PEARLY SHELL! I LOVE YOU! Enjoy your day,okay? God bless!^^</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480570257ra/21324976.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_202781537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202781537" />
    <a title="Sasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5277716-sasha"><img alt="Sasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370179535p2/5277716.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202781537?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sasha" href="/user/show/5277716-sasha">Sasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277716-sasha?shelf=2012-publication">2012-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277716-sasha?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277716-sasha?shelf=2012-debut-author">2012-debut-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277716-sasha?shelf=ya-qc-4">ya-qc-4</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277716-sasha?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202781537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13118627688056979100">The Catastrophic History of You and Me is every girl’s worst nightmare. Brie is dating this awesome guy and they go out to dinner and – BAM – he tells her he doesn’t love her. Next thing she knows, she’s dead. That’s right, she literally DIED of a broken heart. And her dad is a cardiologist so he starts digging into this notion that one can die of a broken heart. But Brie has to go through the stages of grief before she can “move on” to a better place.<br/><br/>This book is definitely cute. It was lighthe</span>
  <span id="freeText13118627688056979100" style="display:none">The Catastrophic History of You and Me is every girl’s worst nightmare. Brie is dating this awesome guy and they go out to dinner and – BAM – he tells her he doesn’t love her. Next thing she knows, she’s dead. That’s right, she literally DIED of a broken heart. And her dad is a cardiologist so he starts digging into this notion that one can die of a broken heart. But Brie has to go through the stages of grief before she can “move on” to a better place.<br /><br />This book is definitely cute. It was lighthearted and fun while dealing with this theme of death. Brie sees how her various family members and friends handle her death and grieve for her loss. Everyone deals with her death in their own way and it was interesting to see how Brie, herself, dealt with her death. 16 is definitely too young to die – I’m sure everyone would agree with that statement.<br /><br />I was really enjoying this book up until about 80% of the way through the book. It took this weird turn that I was confused about. It made a good story and really came full circle for Brie’s counterpart, Patrick, but I was confused on why/how the book got to that point. It’s not that I didn’t like it, it just seemed to come out of nowhere. If you’ve read the book, tell me your thoughts in the comments.<br /><br />Definitely a solid debut and I really enjoyed Jess’s writing. Looking forward to seeing what she comes out with next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13118627688056979100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_276842327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276842327" />
    <a title="Sarah (saz101)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3825460-sarah-saz101"><img alt="Sarah (saz101)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300234087p2/3825460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/276842327?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah (saz101)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah (saz101)" href="/user/show/3825460-sarah-saz101">Sarah (saz101)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=2012-releases">2012-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=wow-i-read-a-non-fantasy">wow-i-read-a-non-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=g-g-g-ghosts">g-g-g-ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer276842327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6720965259343332429">Fifteen is altogether way too young to die. Especially to die of a broken heart. So when sweet, funny, charming Brie is cut down in the prime of her teenage years, what do we get? Angst? A heart-warming Disney movie? Well, perhaps not what you expect. It's more than either. The Catastrophic History of You and Me is brimming with humour and charm and tempered with a perfect balance of heartbreak. <br/><br/><em>Shortly before her sixteenth birthday, Brie Eagan’s boyfriend tells her he doesn’t love her... and sh</em></span>
  <span id="freeText6720965259343332429" style="display:none">Fifteen is altogether way too young to die. Especially to die of a broken heart. So when sweet, funny, charming Brie is cut down in the prime of her teenage years, what do we get? Angst? A heart-warming Disney movie? Well, perhaps not what you expect. It's more than either. The Catastrophic History of You and Me is brimming with humour and charm and tempered with a perfect balance of heartbreak. <br /><br /><em>Shortly before her sixteenth birthday, Brie Eagan’s boyfriend tells her he doesn’t love her... and she dies of a broken heart. No, not figuratively. Her heart <em>literally</em> breaks in two within her chest. True story. Well, the great pizza-parlour in the sky? NOT where she thought she’d wind up. And if she thought her afterlife couldn’t get much weirder than sitting in a vinyl booth eating slices and drinking Sprite, her tour guide to the afterlife is resident Lost Soul, Patrick: an irritating and slightly gorgeous mind-reading boy straight out of the eighties, complete with cheesy jokes and Top-Gun style bomber jacket. Yup. Dying of a broken heart? Just the beginning. If Brie wants to find her happily ever after-life she has to tackle the five stages of grief head-on... and let go of the life she’s not quite ready to leave behind.</em><br /><br />The Catastrophic History of You and Me feels like a contemporary... and I suppose it is, despite its ‘paranormal’ twist. But we’re not talking about vampires and werewolves and supernatural beings... we’re talking about a normal girl, a normal world, and how on earth you come to terms with waking up dead. <br /><br /><b>Brie. Like the Cheese. </b><br />I liked Brie immediately. I loved her humor, her go-to ‘your mom’ jokes when she’s lost for a comeback, her chatty, hyper voice and her constant Disney references. She’s a character you’d have to try hard not to like. She’s layered and she has her own personality, her own dreams, her own aspirations. She has real, deep attachments to the people in her life—her family, her <em>dog</em>, her incredibly close and beautiful circle of best friends. It’s watching her lose these, seeing them fall apart with her gone, then move on, and all along knowing Brie must let go that is so, so heart breaking to watch.<br /><br />This is her story, make no mistake. Her navigating denial, anger, bargaining, sadness and acceptance... and shining throughout. It's wonderful to see a bright, vibrant character as the star of their own show. Whether Brie’s learning to ‘wish’ (wishes are just a matter of willpower in her ‘heaven’), learning to ‘zoom’ from her new plane to our own, or plotting ghostly revenge against one-time loved-ones. Even when she’s lost to her anger, or making terrible, terrible choices in bargaining—regardless of how selfless her motivations—she’s an amazing character. She’s compelling.<br /><br /><b>Deeper Down The Rabbit Hole</b><br />The Catastrophic History of You and Me is a surprisingly complex story. It flies effortlessly from Brie’s longing for her old life, to the grief of her family and friends left behind, to the strange mechanics of the amazing, magical purgatory she finds herself in. On a few occasions I caught glimpses of the amazing magic of <em>Dead Like Me</em>, or Annie’s storyline in <em>Being Human</em>. The detail, the heartbreak, the intensity, and the fun all rang true.<br /><br />The depth of the world and the ‘secondary’ characters is extraordinary. Each and every person in Brie’s world is real and layered and explored in surprising detail. Black and white villains become flawed characters I loved, and forgave along with Brie. Characters—one in particular—I was deeply in love with were hiding secrets subtly hinted at, yet so artfully concealed and unravelled, my unsuspecting heart cracked open and bled at their revelation. So many minute, tiny details come together to create a vividly imagined world coexisting in, beside, and just beyond our own.<br /><br /><b>Verdict</b><br />Sweet, funny, charming, and just a little bit heartbreaking, The Catastrophic History of You and Me sucked me in and, like it’s protagonist, stubbornly refused to let me go. I strongly recommend having a box of tissues and a cuddly, furry animal on standby while you read.<br /><br />Jess Rothenberg creates a magical, quirky and beautiful world. Despite the (many) tears I shed over the course of the book, it’s certainly not a sad book. It’s brimming with hope and joy, and light moments shining through the darkness. It’s about coming to terms with loss, but also about learning to treasure the past while embracing the future. About learning to let go and live the journey... Because, well, <em>to the well-organized mind, death is but the next great adventure.</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="6720965259343332429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_268002063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268002063" />
    <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue"><img alt="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185382p2/4659650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268002063?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=alamw12">alamw12</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=ghosts-revenants-reincarnation">ghosts-revenants-reincarnation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audible-romance-package">audible-romance-package</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268002063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8889129486104354930">This. Book. Wins. If this had been the book given to me as my first foray into comtemporary YA -- and granted, it has supernatural elements, what with the MC being dead and all -- anyway, had this been my first contemporary read, it might have easily led me to decide that contemps were my favorite subgenre. Instead, I've shied away from most anything contemporary and consistently read paranormals with a heavy dose of romance to satisfy my cravings. This book may have changed all that. Don't thin</span>
  <span id="freeText8889129486104354930" style="display:none">This. Book. Wins. If this had been the book given to me as my first foray into comtemporary YA -- and granted, it has supernatural elements, what with the MC being dead and all -- anyway, had this been my first contemporary read, it might have easily led me to decide that contemps were my favorite subgenre. Instead, I've shied away from most anything contemporary and consistently read paranormals with a heavy dose of romance to satisfy my cravings. This book may have changed all that. Don't think that means that I'll forego supernatural stories in favor of lighter, fluffier reads. But I will give all contemps a second thought, instead of immediately dismissing them due to their lack of imaginary beasties.<br /><br />The Catastrophic History of You &amp; Me is not a book I'll soon forget. It's cute, funny, heart-breaking, sad, beautiful, honest, and a whole slew of other adjectives. Pretty much, I ran a full gamut of emotions while reading this novel. I teared up -- okay, bawled like a baby because I tend to be overly sentimental -- twice within the first two chapters alone. But I also laughed -- a lot -- throughout the book. And I swooned...oh, did I swoon.<br /><br />Basically, this book takes you through the five stages of grief (denial, anger, bargaining, sadness, and acceptance) as Brie deals with each of them after her death. And she's got dreamy lost soul Patrick to help her through them. (Cue the swooning.) I absolutely adored the voice given to Brie. She's witty and sarcastic and well, adorable, even when she makes some questionable decisions. But honestly, who among us <i>wouldn't</i> take the opportunity to spy on our loved ones after we're gone?<br /><br />The story was one of redemption, of love lost and found again, and of understanding and compassion when others need it most. I thoroughly enjoyed the subtle hints placed throughout the story, and though I figured out what was really going on half-way through, I was still pleasantly surprised at how it came to fruition. It was slightly predictable without being obvious. Also, the chapters are titled after songs, some of them popular love songs, some of them corny songs from the 80s. And Brie herself is a big fan of 80s music. Because I really needed a reason to love her more. <br /><br />You want to know something else I've decided I like about contemporary novels? A lot of them are stand-alone novels. I love a good series as much as the next girl, but sometimes, you just want to finish a novel in one sitting and revel in that sense of accomplishment, in knowing how the story ends without having to wait for the next installment. So, there's another plus for this story...as if I needed another one. :) I will recommend this debut novel to everyone, and I mean everyone. And if there's any doubt as to why, see the first paragraph of this review again. It's not everyday that a novel can convert me to the lighter side of YA.<br /><br />And now, one of my favorite passages from the book. (Mind you, this is taken from the ARC I received and may not appear in the final version of the novel...but I'll be really sad to find out if it doesn't make the cut.)<br /><br />From pages 42 - 44: <br /><br /> I crossed my arms and clenched my jaw, feeling my inner five-year-old beginning to act out. "I. Don't. Have. A. Pen."<br /> She pointed at my right hand. "Yes. You. Do."<br /> Before I could argue with her, I realized that actually, I did have a pen. Right in my hand, ready to go. I almost fell off my chair.<br /> <i>How the hell did that get there?!</i><br /> The weirdest part? I recognized it.<br /> No. <i>Way.</i><br /> It was the exact same pen I'd had back in third grade. Back when I was an even bigger dork who got so excited I couldn't sleep before School Supply Shopping Day.<br /> The pen was white on top and sky blue on bottom, with six (six!) color options, depending on which button you pushed down. You could even press two buttons down at the same time and mix the colors. (I <i>know</i>.) To a third-grade bookworm who'd spent her entire summer practicing her signature in cursive, this pen was a complete and total thing of beauty.<br /> I'd left it in my desk one Friday afternoon, but when I looked for it the following Monday morning, it was gone. We're talking Real Life Elementary School Tragedy.<br /> But then, in a very suspicious turn of events, Chloe Lutz--a girl who wore her hair in pigtails every day, for god's sake--showed up with a similar (and by similar I mean identical) pen a few days later.<br /> <i>Et tu, Chloe?</i><br /> <i>I</i> knew she took it. Emma, Sadie, and Tess knew she took it. But tattling wasn't an option because our teacher Mrs. Arden had a very harsh No-Tattling policy. I wanted to confront her at recess, but I figured that was a bad idea, considering a) she was a whole foot taller than me and b) she was a brown belt in karate.<br /> In the end, I spent the whole rest of that school year watching Chloe have the time of her life pushing my beloved color buttons. Red! No, blue! Oh, isn't this fun?<br /> <i>Yes, Chloe Slutz, of course it's fun. That is obviously why I bought it.</i><br /> And now, all these years later, here I was in a grungy pizza parlor in Half Moon Bay, dead since Monday, and holding the very same World's Greatest Pen.<br /> <i>SO weird.</i><br /><br />First, <i>I had that pen</i>! Second, I think that passage highlights how funny and normal Brie is, and it gives you a little insight into her character.<br /><br />Not a huge fan of the trailer, but here it is anyway: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://youtu.be/UvnmX3ywXYY">http://youtu.be/UvnmX3ywXYY</a><br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2012/02/review-catastrophic-history-of-you-me.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8889129486104354930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/6180856-celine">Celine</a>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141334479" href="/book/show/13411612-the-catastrophic-history-of-you-and-me">review of another edition</a>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288227252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12485045919246289548">Review originally posted in: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://forget8me8not.blogspot.com.au/2012/04/85-book-review-catastrophic-history-of.html'>http://forget8me8not.blogspot.com.au/...</a><br/><br/><u>Cover:</u><br/>I love the girl's purple dress , the sky background and the upside down bridge. She died because of a broken heart. Her heart LITERALLY broke in half...</b><br/><br/><b>don't you (forget about me)</b><br/><br/>I don't think I'll even bother writing my own synopsis for this book. What I'll do instead is put some of </span>
  <span id="freeText12485045919246289548" style="display:none">Review originally posted in: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://forget8me8not.blogspot.com.au/2012/04/85-book-review-catastrophic-history-of.html">http://forget8me8not.blogspot.com.au/...</a><br /><br /><u>Cover:</u><br />I love the girl's purple dress , the sky background and the upside down bridge. I can feel as if the girl is flying there in the sky and the cover gives off this heaven and calm feeling!<br /><br /><u>Story:</u><br /><br /><b>There's a girl called Brie. She died because of a broken heart. Her heart LITERALLY broke in half...</b><br /><br /><b>don't you (forget about me)</b><br /><br />I don't think I'll even bother writing my own synopsis for this book. What I'll do instead is put some of the chapter titles of the book along with my review! I had high expectations for The Catastrophic History of You and Me, considering all the positive reviews I've been reading about this book and how so many people love it. The Catastrophic History of You and Me is beyond my expectations. This book was so awesome and amazing. The idea of someone who died because their heart literally broke in half (like really broke in half) is so unique. <br /><br /><b>what becomes of the broken hearted?</b><br /><br />It must have been really painful for Brie when her heart broke in half when she died. Before I even read the story, the way the pages of the book are set and the chapter titles made me fall in love with this book. <br /><br /><b>excuse me while I kiss the sky</b><br /><br />YES! This book is so touching, and well-written. It is filled with so many emotions. It's fun, it's sad, it's beautiful, it's hilarious and it gives you this warm fuzzy feeling when you read the book. The book is split into 5 parts and I love the stories in each part. Not only that, I LOVE THE CHAPTER TITLES. They are from song lyrics and they're PERFECT. This book touched me in ways I never thought of. I love it. It's amazing. The ending is perfect.<br /><br /><b>permanently black and blue, permanently blue, for you</b> <br /> <br /><u>Characters:</u><br /><br /><b>somewhere over the rainbow</b><br /><br />There is Patrick. He's a Darling. Hey, no pun intended. He is Patrick Darling. (Yes, Darling is his surname!). He is adorable, he's amazing, he's awesome and I fall in love with him. I'd willingly break my heart in half if it means I can see him! He's the coolest character ever. He wears leather brown jacket, and rides motorcycle. He is sweet, charming and oh, what I'd do to make him smile. <br /><br /><b>only the good die young</b><br /><br />Patrick is nearly 18 when he died! 17 years is not enough to see the beauty of the world and to feel love.<br /><br /><b>the cheese stands alone</b><br /> <br />Brie stands for Aubrie. Brie is the name of a cheese and yes, she stands alone! She is such a fun character to read about. I connected with her in every ways and understand her pain of being told that her own boyfriend that he did not love her and the pain of not being able to live in the world any longer. <br /><br /><b>1,2,3,4, tell me that you love me more</b><br /><br />I love Brie and Patrick's relationship. They are so perfect for each other. There is an attraction from the very first moment they saw each other but they came to love each other after the time they spent together. <br /><br /><b>who will save your soul if you won’t save your own?</b><br /><br />I loved the other characters such as Brie's family and friends. Brie's BFFs totally rocks. They are friends that stay with you forever, no matter what happens. Jacob, Brie's boyfriend who broke her heart was a character that completely surprised me. I wanted to know why he broke up with her, seeing how he and Brie were so lovey-dovey in their relationship and when I found out what the reason was, I wanted to hug him. <br /><br /><b>to die by your side, is such a heavenly way to die</b><br /><br />I love the characters. They make me filled with so many beautiful emotions I want to hold on to. <br /><br /><u>Overall:</u><br />The Catastrophic History of You and Me is a book that will fill you with so many beautiful emotions you want to hold on to forever. The darling Patrick and the cute Brie will take you on a journey to find out what it's like when your heart literally broke in half, what it means to be in denial, to be angry, to bargain, to feel sadness and to accept death. This is one my favourite 2012 debut novels!<br /><br />And I'll close my review with one chapter title:<br /><br /><b>all you need is love</b><br /><br /><b>Thank you Penguin Australia for the review copy!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12485045919246289548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289525192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2998921403290058800">So...<br/>I'll admit it from the get-go: <br/>this book started out sort of 'meh' for me. I was not really 'feeling it' and I sort of found the heroine a bit whiny, self-absorbed, and a little too vengeful and agressive for my taste. My main complaints would be along these lines, 'Don't blame the world for your problems honey', 'dont judge and jump to conclusions' and'don't take your anger out on others'.<br/><br/>BUT about a 3rd of my way into the book though, things started to change. The story got a hold of me, </span>
  <span id="freeText2998921403290058800" style="display:none">So...<br>I'll admit it from the get-go: <br>this book started out sort of 'meh' for me. I was not really 'feeling it' and I sort of found the heroine a bit whiny, self-absorbed, and a little too vengeful and agressive for my taste. My main complaints would be along these lines, 'Don't blame the world for your problems honey', 'dont judge and jump to conclusions' and'don't take your anger out on others'.<br><br>BUT about a 3rd of my way into the book though, things started to change. The story got a hold of me, I got invested in the characters that were coming alive on the pages, and the story seemed to have more depth than I initiallly thought, and I just wanted to keep on reading to see where this was all leading them, and me, since I was now fully on-board with it.<br><br>Then towards the end, at about the last 3rd or so of the book I was a lost cause. The characters had shown some actual growth, the story had unfolded itself beautifully, even if on some aspects anticipated, and I <b> did not want the book to end </b> which is a pretty good sign, that a book has managed to really get a hold on me.<br><br>It grew from a 3 - to a 4 - to a 5 star reading experience for me, and knowing what I know now, and if I were to re-read it, I doubt the beginning would seem like a 3 anymore.<br><br>Without saying too much, i can say this:<br>This book is both sad, funny, sweet - at points trivial, at others deep - with flawed characters that make mistakes, but who learns and grows, and are able to apologise and forgive, who are both fighting change and embracing it, - and this book weaves it together beautifully, and it left me not able to get it out of my mind (not that I really wanted to), even when the last page had been turned (which is another one of those signs of a good reading experience).<br>So if that sounds like the sort of book you like to read, I suggest you give it a try. And if you do, my only advice, will be this:<b> have patience </b>. Sometimes you have to get to know people better, to understand them, and sometimes you have to give people (including yourself) time to evolve and struggle with things before they can be resolved. <br><br>A book well-written, well-plotted, and well-told and I'm surely coming back to read more of Rothenbergs work.<br><br>So let me just end by saying this:<br><br><a href="http://s1154.photobucket.com/albums/p527/mizzsandie/?action=view&amp;current=sorrywaswrong.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380371630ra/724761.gif" alt="i was wrong okay? i was wrong!" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272334220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10896781790270506596">At the beginning of the novel, the main character introduced her sisterhood of the corny metaphorical necklace by comparing them to Disney princesses. One exotic, one redhead with a pet crab and one brunette who loves to read. Wanna take a shot which princesses are those? This is only one of the many examples of lazy writing that is so prevalent in this thing that pains me to call a novel.<br/><br/>It is so full of those baits you commonly see on 'reviews' that contain lines like "Plus, you'll really love</span>
  <span id="freeText10896781790270506596" style="display:none">At the beginning of the novel, the main character introduced her sisterhood of the corny metaphorical necklace by comparing them to Disney princesses. One exotic, one redhead with a pet crab and one brunette who loves to read. Wanna take a shot which princesses are those? This is only one of the many examples of lazy writing that is so prevalent in this thing that pains me to call a novel.<br /><br />It is so full of those baits you commonly see on 'reviews' that contain lines like "Plus, you'll really love [insert name of adorable young sibling]" or "ZOMG Cute and Smart Doggie." or worse, "[Name of Love Interest] &lt;3 &lt;3". It's fluff, the unhealthy kind.<br /><br />I could go on and on on how this made death so utterly ridiculous. It is an unholy, melodramatic, corny, lazily written and incredibly naive shitshow. Avoid like the plague.</span>

<div id="review_412473277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412473277" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7373882-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412473277?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/7373882-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=books-library-owns">books-library-owns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412473277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer860819149400632335"><b>You can obsess and obsess over how things ended - what you did wrong or could have done differently - but there's not much of a point. It's not like it'll change anything. So really, why worry?</b><br/><br/>I was thinking about giving this only 3 stars, but no. It deserves 4.<br/><br/>This book was amazing in so many ways. I was drawn in from the first sentence. (I got bored for a few pages, but whatever. That's nothing compared to how I felt about the rest of the book.) After the not-so-interesting part, this book jus</span>
  <span id="freeText860819149400632335" style="display:none"><b>You can obsess and obsess over how things ended - what you did wrong or could have done differently - but there's not much of a point. It's not like it'll change anything. So really, why worry?</b><br /><br />I was thinking about giving this only 3 stars, but no. It deserves 4.<br /><br />This book was amazing in so many ways. I was drawn in from the first sentence. (I got bored for a few pages, but whatever. That's nothing compared to how I felt about the rest of the book.) After the not-so-interesting part, this book just got better and better.<br /><br /><b>The trouble is, sometimes words are like arrows. Once you shoot them, there's no going back.</b><br /><br />I loved the characters. Brie is very... real. I can relate to her (not about her broken heart, heh), something that doesn't happen with many other characters. Although she is dense at times, she was funny and I grew to really like her. Her five stages of grief were fun to read.<br /><br />Who I loved more is Patrick. Sure, he's cheesy, but he made me laugh. He and Brie have a great relationship, and I love how everything ties together in the end. I want someone like Patrick in my life. Even if he does dress from the 80s.<br /><br />There was one character that didn't come up as much as Brie or Patrick, for obvious reasons, but I absolutely <i>loved</i>. Brie's dog, Hamloaf. He would randomly (or maybe not) appear and omg, he’s hilarious. I’m not a dog person, not an animal person at all, but I would totally go for a dog like Hamloaf. His name alone is wonderful.<br /><br /><b>No matter how much you think you know a person - no matter how pretty they act, or how popular they seem, you can never know what their lives are really like.</b><br /><br />I really liked that this wasn't predictable. I didn't see that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Brie was actually Lily, the girl Patrick committed suicide over <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <i>The Catastrophic History of You and Me</i> kept me reading until the end. It’s light-hearted, and I would definitely recommend this book.<br /><br /><b>Sometimes, friends drift in and out of our lives like fashion accessories - in one season and out the next.”</b> (SO TRUE.)<br /><br />*Half a star goes to using song titles for the chapters. That's brilliant.<br /><br /><b>When you're in love, the world is brighter. Sunnier. The air smells flowerier, and your hair is silkier, and suddenly you find yourself smiling at babies and strangers and old couples walking down the beach holding hands.</b><br /><br />And so I was reading the acknowledgements (do people do that anymore?), and I loved the last one.<br /><i>Finally, to all the boys—from preschool and beyond—who ever broke my heart: Thanks for everything. Revenge may be sweet, but book deals are definitely sweeter.</i><br />I love that last line.<br /><br /><b>Turns out, hell's not so much a burning, scalding pit of fire and misery. It's actually much, much worse than that. Hell is when the people you love the most reach right into your soul and rip it out of you. And they do it because they can.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="860819149400632335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_211916365" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211916365" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211916365?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844873-laura?shelf=cover-me">cover-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211916365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2215385038824026945"><br/><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>The Catastrophic History of You and Me is a jolt to the heart! Love is on full display in the pages of this book. All of love’s lovely little pockets and hidden away dark corners. Everything love has to offer is here. Blushing, beaming joy to brutal, heart crushing agony! Love isn’t always rainbows and romance. Just ask Brie.<br/><br/><b>“Love hurts us all, no matter how old or young we are.”</b><br/><br/>Brie Eagan died of a broken heart. Really. She’s dead. But <s>life</s>…<i>well</i> the afterlife must go on. We follow Brie</span>
  <span id="freeText2215385038824026945" style="display:none"><br /><b>4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />The Catastrophic History of You and Me is a jolt to the heart! Love is on full display in the pages of this book. All of love’s lovely little pockets and hidden away dark corners. Everything love has to offer is here. Blushing, beaming joy to brutal, heart crushing agony! Love isn’t always rainbows and romance. Just ask Brie.<br /><br /><b>“Love hurts us all, no matter how old or young we are.”</b><br /><br />Brie Eagan died of a broken heart. Really. She’s dead. But <s>life</s>…<i>well</i> the afterlife must go on. We follow Brie on a journey of memories, denial, anger, longing, acceptance, and LOVE in a new and ever changing landscape that I don’t want to spoil for you with too many details. Let's just say the afterlife is a new world with rules and ways all its own. Good thing this new world comes with a guide! :)<br /><br />Meet the cocky and charming, Patrick, the Resident Lost Soul of Brie’s particular slice of heaven. Brie and Patrick are so much fun to watch. They jab and joke and *spark* at first eye lock! From every cheesy nickname in the book to fun, flirty banter—these two have it going on! So much fun. Could they be more than friends though? How could they? Brie’s heart is broken. Broken hearts don’t fall in love again. Do they?<br /><br />If you have ever been in love and had your heart shattered into itty bitty pieces, this book is for you. The power of this story really surprised me. Hidden underneath the sarcasm and humor and flirty ways is a mountain of emotion. Heartbreak. Heartache. Anger. Fear. Joy. Patience. Tenderness. Love, love and love. It’s all in here! Every element comes to light in Brie’s relationships with her family, friends, and more. Come listen to her heart. It may be broken, but it’s still thump-thump-thumping away.<br /><br />And then we have the music to listen to, hum along with, and remember. Ms. Rothenberg’s chapter titles are songs and lines that make me smile. Oh how they make me smile! I’ve had ooh Heaven Is a Place on Earth and Lucky Star in my head for days! :D Most of the shout outs are 80s tunes, so prepared to be blasted back into the past!<br /><br />This book opened up a well of old feelings and memories in me. Some happy, some not so happy. But isn’t that one of the many joys of reading. I adore a book that makes me examine old loves and hurts and joys. I’ll be on the lookout for more from Jess Rothenberg for sure.<br /><br />I highly recommend this dazzling journey through life and death showcasing the power of love.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2215385038824026945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
